(c) Do. do. £7 16 10 do. 29 REPORT OF THE COUNCIL of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth For the Year ended. 31st March, 1909. 1. At the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November, Election of Councillor Archibald Davis Dawnay was unaniMayor. mously elected Mayor of the Borough for the year 1908-9. 2. On the same day it was unanimously Resolved :— The Ex- " That the best thanks of the Council be given to Alderman Mayor. John William Lorden, J.P., for is able, courteous, and impartial conduct in the Chair, and for the time and attention bestowed by him in the discharge of his duties as Mayor of the Borough and as a Justice of the Peace during the year 1907-8." A copy of the foregoing resolution was sealed with the Common Seal of the Council and handed to Alderman Lorden. 3. At the same Meeting the Mayor (Councillor Archibald D. Dawnay), on behalf of subscribers (Members and Ex-Members of the Council), presented to Alderman Lorden his portrait in oils, painted by Mr. C. E. Butler, and a replica thereof by the same artist. The portrait having been unveiled by the Mayoress, Alderman Lorden thanked the subscribers and presented one of the portraits to the Council. The Mayor accepted the portrait on behalf of the Council, and it is now hung in the Council Chamber. 4. On the same occasion Councillor Wise, on behalf of the Presentation subscribers (Members of the Council), presented to to Mayoress. Mrs. Lorden three silver fruit dishes as a mark of appreciation of her services in the discharge of the duties of Mayoress during the past year. 30 5. The Council regret to record the deaths on the 13th October, 1908, of Alderman Rucker: on the 10th Obituary. February, 1909, of Councillor Palmer; on the 8th March, 1909, of Councillor Law; on the 19th February, 1909, of Mr. T. P. Ling; and on the 7th March, 1909, of Mr. J. Y. Henderson. Alderman Rucker had been a Member of the Council since its establishment in 1900. He was a regular attendant at Council and Committee Meetings; an active and generous supporter of philanthropic and other public institutions, and the valuable services which he rendered to the Borough for so many years are highly appreciated. Councillor Palmer had also been a Member of the Council since 1900, and regularly attended the Council and Committee Meetings. Councillor Law had been a Member of the Council since November, 1906. Mr. T. P. Ling was a Member from 1900 to 1906; and Mr. J. Y. Henderson from December, 1900, to November, 1903. 6. On the 2nd December the Council elected Councillor J. H. Election of Anderson, M.A., an Alderman of the Borough, to Alderman fill the vacancy caused by the death of Alderman Rucker. 7. An election to fill the vacancy caused by the election of Casual Councillor Anderson as Alderman was held on the Vacancy. 29th January, when the votes recorded were as follows, viz. :— Name of Candidate. No. of Votes recoided. Hallett, John Wright 766 (Elected) Joy, Herbert. 94 Limb, Joseph Johnson ( 228 8. The number of Electors, the number of Electors voting-, etc., were as follows, viz. :— Number of Electors. Number of Electors voting. Percentage of Electors voting. Number of rejected Ballot Papers. 5727 1094 1910 6 31 9. The popularity of the Tooting Public Library which was Tooting Public presented to the Council by Sir William Lancaster Library. in 1902 having outgrown its capacity, Sir William kindly offered to bear the cost of extending it by adding a second storey. By this addition there is provided a capacious reading room and two magazine rooms, thus allowing the former reading and magazine room on the ground floor to be converted into a lending library, and the old lending library into a reference library. The offer of Sir William was communicated to the Council on the 6th May, 1908, when the following resolution was passed, viz. :— "That the best thanks of the Council be presented to Sir Wm. Lancaster, J.P., L.C.C., for his munificent offer to provide an addition to the Tooting Library, which he so generously presented to the Borough in 1902." 10. The additions were carried out under the supervision of and in accordance with plans prepared by Alderman W. Hunt, J.P., L.C.C. During the progress of the work the business of the library was carried on in the Boys' School Room, Church Lane, Tooting, and the library was re-opened on the 3rd December last. 11. The Council has pleasure in recording the fact that, Sir Frederick amongst the Birthday Honours, H.M. The King Lance, K.C.B. conferred the distinction of Knight Commander of the Most Honourable Order of the Bath upon General Lance, C.B., who has been a Member of the Council since 1900. 12. The Mayor, Aldermen, Councillors and principal officers Church Council attended in State services at the Services. following Churches in the Borough, viz. :— 6th Dec., 1908 Parish Church of Wandsworth, All Saints', High Street. 3rd Jan., 1909 Parish Church of Clapham, Holy Trinity, Clapham Common. 24th Jan., 1909 Parish Church of Putney, St. Mary, High Street. 14th Feb., 1909 St. Saviour's Church, Cedars Road, Clapham. 14th March, 1909 Parish Church of Streatham, St. Leonard, Streatham High Road. •9th May, 1909 Parish Church of Tooting, St. Nicholas, Church Lane. 32 13. The Council also attended, on the 10th June, 1908, the institution of the Rev. Prebendary Dalton as Rector of Clapham at the Clapham Parish Church. 14. The draft of the Scheme of the Charity Commissioners Weir Hospital reference to the Weir Hospital Trust, referred Trust- to in the last Annual Report, was received in July last, when a Special Committee of the Council was appointed to consider the matter. The following report of the Committee was adopted by the Council on the 23rd September, 1908, viz. :— 1. We have considered the proposed Scheme of the Charity Commissioners for the administration of the Weir Hospital Charity. 2. The Scheme is practically the same as that proposed by a majority of the Trustees and former Committee of Management, which was the subject of the Public Inquiry held by Mr. H. A. Baker, Assistant Commissioner, at Balham, on the 5th and 8th November last, when it was strongly objected to by the numerous inhabitants of Streatham who attended or were represented there. 3. The proposed expenditure of 50,000 of the Capital Funds of the Charity for completing and equipping the blocks of buildings of the Bolingbroke Hospital, situate in the Borough of Battersea, is contrary to the terms of Mr. Weir's Will, which contemplates a capital expenditure out of the accumulated income of such funds only, and for a dissimilar purpose. The Testator clearly directed that The Hawthorns, Grove Road, Balham, should be established as a Hospital, to be called the Weir Hospital, and did not intend to benefit any existing institution, more especially one not situate in Streatham. The expenditure of this sum of £0,000 would absorb more than one-half of the present value of the Charity Funds. 4. The Scheme would place the control of the Funds in the hands of a body consisting of eighteen members, of whom only six would be chosen in a similar way to that prescribed by the Will. The Scheme gives no indication of the manner in which the twelve other members are to be chosen. 5. The proposal to establish a home for forty nurses is not only not provided for by the Testator's Will, but as only three of the nurses would render gratuitous service it would not even be using the Funds for a charitable purpose. Trained nurses can be obtained by persons requiring them, at existing institutions. 6. As the Scheme is fundamentally opposed to the views set out in the Memorial to the Charity Commissioners, sealed by the Council on the 4th December last (a copy of which accompanies this report), it appears to us that it would serve no good purpose to suggest amendments to its details. We may, however, point out that the Scheme omits to provide (which it should do) for the annual expenditure of £20 for repairs to St. Mary's Church, Balham, or for the maintenance of Mr. Weir's tablet in that 33 Church, and of his grave and monument at Nunhead Cemetery, or for the annual sermon—all of which are prescribed by the Will. 7. The Scheme is in effect a diversion of tne funds for the benefit of the Bolingbroke Hospital, and is contrary to the directions of the Testator. It has not been shown—and in our opinion it cannot be shown—that it is not possible to apply the Funds in the way in which the Testator has directed them to be applied, and the Scheme is therefore wrong in law. 8. We have had an opportunity of considering a Scheme for the administration of the Charity which was submitted to the Charity Commissioners by the present Committee of Management in January last, which proposes to establish a Dispensary, Nurses' Home, and two small Casualty Wards, on the site of Mr. Weir's house, The Hawthorns, Grove Road, Balham, and includes a provis on for the maintenance in convalescent homes in the country, or at the seaside, of inhabitants of Streatham and the neighbourhood, including local patients discharged from general hospitals, who may be certified for such treatment by the Weir Dispensary Medical Officers. We approve of this Scheme, but we suggest that, in addition, an ambulance or ambulances should be provided at The Hawthorns, as proposed by the draft Scheme of the Charity Commissioners. The Committee of Management suggest, further, that by the accumulation of unexpended income a similar institution should at a future time be established in the southern part of Streatham. We also approve of this suggestion. 9. We recommend :— (a) That the Council suggest that the draft Scheme be amended by incorporating in it the above-mentioned proposals of the Committee of Management of January last, and by leaving out all reference to the Bolingbroke Hospital; and by providing (b) That the control and management of the Charity should be in accordance with the directions contained in the Will. (c) That it be referred to us to consider any further action which may be taken by the Charity Commissioners in the matter, and to recommend the taking of any such proceedings by the Council as we may be advised are necessary in opposing the Scheme of the Charity Commissioners and to secure the carrying into effect of the foregoing recommendations. 15. A copy of the foregoing report was forwarded to the Charity Commissioners, as the objections and suggestions of the Council upon the draft Scheme. 16. In December, the Charity Commissioners having published their Scheme for the administration of the Charity in substantially the same form as drafted, the Council applied to the Commissioners for authority to present a petition to the High 34 Court of Chancery against the Scheme. This authority was given, and the necessary steps are being taken to prosecute the appeal. 17. Alderman Hewett, and Councillors Anderson and Garrett, Junr., whose term of office expired on the 10th October last, were re-appointed the Council's representatives on the Committee of Management of the Weir Hospital Trust for the current year. 18. In September, 1908, a letter was received from the Putney Charity Commissioners suggesting that, in view of Charities. small endowment of the Putney Pest House Charity, so large a body of Trustees as at present was not necessary and that the body should consist of the Rector and the Ward representatives, that a scheme should be made to effect this alteration, and to vest the legal estate of the Charity in the Official Trustees of Charity Lands. This Council concurred in the opinion that the present Body of Trustees is too large, and recommended that the Trustees should be the Vicar and Churchwardens, exofficio, and nine persons to be appointed by the Councillors for the Putney Ward. The Charity Commissioners have not yet made any order in the matter. 19. In January, 1909, the Charity Commissioners proposed to Streatham establish a scheme for varying the scheme regulatCharities. ing non-ecclesiastical charities of Streatham, so as to provide that the number of pensioners may be increased if and as the charity permits, and that the receipt of Poor Law medical relief shall not disqualify a person from being an almsperson or pensioner of the Charity. The matter is under consideration. 20. Councillor Campbell was re-appointed a Representative Wandsworth Trustee of the Wandsworth Consolidated Charities Chanties for four years from the 13th April, 1908. In October, 1908, it having been reported to the Council that Alderman Lorden being no longer resident in Springfield Ward there was a vacancy as a Representative Trustee for that Ward, and that there was a vacancy for the Southfield Ward in consequence of the death of Alderman Rucker, the Council, on the 4th November, appointed Councillor Wise a Representative Trustee for the Springfield Ward, and Alderman Lorden a Representative Trustee for the Southfield Ward for a period of four years. 35 21. Councillor Campbell having resigned his position as a Wandsworth Representative of the Council on the Governing Technical institute. Body of the Wandsworth Technical Institute, the Council, on the 6th May, appointed Councillor Wise to fill the vacancy. 22. Councillor Lidiard, who had been for six years this Metropolitan Council's Representative on the Metropolitan Water Board. Water Board, resigned that position on the 26th March last, and the Council expressed its appreciation of his valuable services by passing the following resolution, viz. :— "That this Council has received with much regret the resignation of Councillor Lidiard as its representative on the Metropolitan Water Board. Councillor Lidiard has been a Member of the Board since its incorporation in 1903, and by his special knowledge of the subject of the water supply of the Metropolis was able to render great assistance in bringing into operation the Act of 1902, under which the various Metropolitan Water Companies were dissolved and their powers and duties transferred to the new Authority. This Council records its high appreciation of the valuable services which Councillor Lidiard has rendered, especially to this Borough, during his six years' Membership of the Water Board, and its sincere thanks for the ability and constant attention shown by him in the discharge of the laborious duties which devolved upon him during that time. The Council further desires to recognize the great service given to the public by Councillor Lidiard, as the first Mayor of the Borough and as a Member of this Council and of its predecessor, the District Board of Works, for the long period of twenty-five years." 23. On the 7th April the Council unanimously elected Alderman Lorden its Representative on the Metropolitan Water Board to fill the vacancy. 24. With the view of making the Wandsworth Town Hall Wandsworth more suitable for letting the room lately used as a Town Hall. General Office for the Rating Department and the small hall have been converted into one room. The walls of the entrance hall and staircase have been tiled and other works of decoration carried out; and the scale of charges has been revised. 25. Several firms having withdrawn their tenders for works, after acceptance by the Council, the following Withdrawal of Tenders. standing Order was passed, viz. :— "That the Council will not accept the tender of any person or firm who shall on any previous occasion have withdrawn a tender after the same has been opened by the Council or a Committee, unless the reasons for the withdrawal were satisfactory to the Council." 36 26. Alderman Robinson and Councillors Sir Frederick Lance Motor and Taylor were appointed this Council's RepresenOmnibuses. tatives to attend a Conference convened by the Poplar Borough Council to consider the subject of the excessive speed at which motor omnibuses are driven in the Metropolis. The following" resolutions were passed, viz. :— 1. That, having regard to the conditions of street traffic in London and the many accidents that have occurred, due to the speed at which motor omnibuses arc driven, this Conference is of opinion that in the interests of the safety of the public it is necessary the speed of motor omnibuses should be further limited in the London area. The Conference therefore urges the Local Government Board to amend Articles IV. of the Heavy Motor Car Order, 1904, so as to restrict the maximum speed of motor omnibuses within the County of London, outside the four-miles radius to 10 miles per hour, and within the four-miles radius to eight miles per hour. 2. That, in the opinion of this Conference, the maximum speed of motor cars passing through the County of London should be restricted to 15 miles per hour, and that representations be made to the Local Government Board to this effect. 3. That representations be made to the Home Secretary and the Chief •Commissioner of Police, as follows, viz. :— (a) That, in the opinion of this Conference, it is desirable the Chief Commissioner of Police should be empowered to require, as a condition of the issue of a license for a motor omnibus or motor cab, the provision of a speed indicator of approved design. (b) That the various Motor Omnibus Companies should be compelled to adopt effective mud guards to remedy the intolerable nuisance to which pedestrians, and residents on the frontages, are subjected through the mud thrown up by the wheels of motor omnibuses in wet weather. 27. This Council decided to support resolution 3 (a), and made no order with reference to the others. 28. This Council considered a report of the Local Government Representation Records and Museums Committee of the London on County Council as to what steps can be taken to re-adjust the representations of County Electoral areas in London in order to remove the present inequalities of representation under which areas differing greatly in population and electorate return the same number of representatives. The report recommended 37 that application be made to Parliament in the Session of 1909 to amend the Local Government Act, 1888, so as to provide:— (1) As from 1st January, 1910, the areas of the Battersea, Clapham, Fulham, Lewisham, Wandsworth, and Woolwich Electoral Divisions of the Administrative County of London shall be sub-divided as follows:— Battersea 2 divisions. Clapham 2 „ Fulham 2 ,, Lewisham 2 „ Wandsworth 3 ,, Woolwich 2 „ (2) Each of such new electoral divisions shall return two Members to serve on the County Council. 38 Existing Electoral division and proposed new divisions. This Council approved of the foregoing proposals, which were considered by the County Council in October last, when such Council decided that the Government should be approached with a view to legislation being introduced in the present Session to effect the suggested amendment of the Local Government Act, and that, failing action by the Government, the Council should endeavour to secure the introduction of a private Member's Bill for the purpose. No Bill on the subject has yet been introduced into Parliament. 30. The Council considered some additions proposed by the Westminster City Council to be made to the lations for costermongers made by the Commissioner of Police, and approved thereof, and appointed Councillors Turnbull and Wise its representatives to attend a Conference convened by the Westminster Council on the subject. The Conference was held on the 16th June, and certain additional regulations, with which this Council agree, were approved and forwarded to the Home Secretary and the Commissioner of Police. Costermongers. 31. The Council again had under consideration the subject of compounding for rates. It was found that since the compounding allowance was reduced from 25 to 20 per cent, in April, 1907, the number of rateable hereditaments in respect of which the owners, rated under Section 4 of the Act of 1869, declined to pay rates whether the premises were occupied or not, had increased from 2,205 to 6,516, and the Rating Committee pointed out that in those cases the owners received 15 per cent, allowance for occupied properties and paid no rates for "empties." The Council, being of opinion that such an arrangement was not of advantage to the Borough, rescinded the resolutions ordering owners to be rated under Section 4 of the Act, and decided that all agreements to compound be under Section 3, and upon condition that all compoundable properties in the Borough belonging to the same owner be included in the agreement; that the maximum rateable value of properties compounded for be £15; that the commission to owners agreeing to become liable for and pay the rates whether the hereditaments be occupied or not, be 15 per cent.; and that unless the rates be paid by the 15th day of the second month in the quarter in which they are due the commission be reduced to 5 per cent. The limit of rateable value c Compounding for Rates. 40 of compoundable property was, however, subsequently altered from £15 to £20. 32. In February last the Council considered a letter from the Chairman of the Territorial Force Association, County of London, asking- for the co-operation of the Council in the endeavour of the association to raise 28,000 men in the County for the Force. A Committee, consisting of the Mayor, Aldermen Anderson and Lorden, and Councillor Sir Frederick Lance, was appointed to deal with the matter. A public meeting was held at the Wandsworth Town Hall on the 16th March, at which the Mayor presided, and other meetings were held in different parts of the Borough with the view of increasing: the Territorial Force in London. Territorial Force. 33. The Council has on several occasions considered the subJect of the desirability of the promotion of a Bill to provide for the superannuation of its officers and servants. The Superannuation Allowances Act, 1866, authorized the Council to grant superannuation allowances to its officers without contributions from the officers, and it had been the practice of the Council and its predecessor, the late Wandsworth District Board of Works, to grant such allowances upon the scale set out in the Act. The Council also granted superannuation allowances to its workmen in accordance with a scale adopted in 1902. It was, however, doubtful whether the Council had power to superannuate workmen. Seven of the Metropolitan Borough Councils had obtained Acts of Parliament for the superannuation of their officers and servants and, having considered those Acts, this Council decided to promote a Bill in the same terms as the St. Marylebone Act, with any necessary modifications. The Bill was accordingly introduced in the Session of 1909, and received the Royal Assent on the 25th May last. The Act comes into force on the 31st March next, and steps are being taken by the Council to bring it into operation. The principal provisions of the Act are :— Superannuation Act. (a) Every officer or servant placed upon the permanent establishment who shall have completed 10 years service and become incapable of discharging his duties with efficiency by reason of permanent infirmity of mind or body, or of old age, or who shall have attained the age of 60 years and completed 40 years' service, shall be entitled, on ceasing to hold his office or employment, to receive out of the Superannuation Fund a 41 superannuation allowance of one-sixtieth af the average amount of his salary or wages and emoluments for each year's service. (b) Superannuation allowances to officers and servants who at the commencement of the Act have attained 65 years of age, or 60 years and have completed 40 years' service, are to be paid out of the General Rate, and not out of the Superannuation Fund. (c) Officers and servants ceasing to hold office in consequence of misconduct forfeit all claim to superannuation. The Council may, however, return to them part or all of their contributions. (d) Officers and servants who resign before being entitled to superannuation, or lose their office or employment by reason of reduction of staff, or cease to hold their office or employment by reason of bodily injury not occasioned by their own default, are entitled to receive a sum equal to the amount of their contributions, and the Council (except in the case of voluntary resignation) may also grant them a gratuity not exceeding two years' salary or wages. (e) In the event of an officer or servant dying before being entitled to superannuation the Council is to pay to his legal personal representatives a sum not exceeding the amount of all, and not less than one-half, of the contributions of such officer or servant. (f) The contributions of officers and servants are as follows, viz. :— With less than five years' service at the commencement of the Act, 2 per cent, of salaries or wages. With more than five years' service, 2½ per cent, of salaries or wages. With more than 15 years' service, 3 per cent, of salaries or wages. (g) The Superannuation Fund to be formed under the Act consists of : (i.) The primary annual contribution out of the General Rate. (ii.) The contributions of officers and servants. (iii.) Dividends and interest arising out of the income of the fund ; and (iv.) Such amount of the General Rate as may be required to meet any deficiency. (h) An actuarial investigation is to be made every five years to fix the primary annual contribution above-mentioned, and this is not to be less than £400. 34. Part III. of this Bill contained similar provisions with regard to unwholesome milk to those contained in the General Powers Bill of last year, and withdrawn because of the Statement that the Government proposed to introduce general legislation on the subject of milk supply. These provisions would authorize the Medical Officer of the London County Council to take, at any railway station, samples of milk for examination, and the Medical Officer of Health of any Sanitary Authority to take samples of milk sold, offered or exposed or deposited for sale at any place (not being a railway station) within the district, and, provided that if such milk should be found to contain any matter rendering it unwholesome or unfit for food, the person producing or consigning it would be liable to a penalty of 40s. for a first, and /~5 for a subsequent conviction. The provisions would also empower the London County Council to prohibit the supply of milk within the County from any dairy outside the County from which the unwholesome milk was supplied. London County Council (General Powers;. 40. That mittee reported that the preamble of the first-mentioned Bill was not proved, and amended the London Electric Supply Bill so as to authorize undertakers and electric lighting companies to enter into agreements for mutual assistance, and to connect mains, and to provide that every power to purchase any undertaking of a supply company which, but for the Act, would be exerciseable by a Local Authority in any part of London, shall be transferred to the London County Council, that such Council shall also be empowered to purchase all the electric lighting undertakings in the County not purchaseable by a Local Authority. The County Council is to give three years' notice of its intention to purchase, and is not to purchase one undertaking London and District Electric Supply, and London Electric Supply. 45 unless at the same time it purchases the whole of the electric lighting undertakings in the County; the undertakings, if purchased, are to be paid for upon the terms in Section 2 of the Electric Lighting Act, 1888. The County Council may proceed to purchase in August, 1931, or at the expiration of any subsequent 10 years, and may discharge not more than three-fourths of the purchase-money by the issue to the company of London County stock. The power of the Corporation of London and the Camberwell Borough Council to purchase the electric lighting undertakings in their respective areas is retained until August, 1927, and the power of the Lambeth Borough Council to re-purchase the undertaking in that Borough is retained until 1928. If not purchased before those dates the power to purchase is to be transferred to the County Council. The Bill, as amended, received the Royal Assent on the 21st December last. 45. This Bill proposed to repeal certain provisions of the Cornpany's Acts relating to the price of gas, dividends and profits, and provides that the standard rate of dividend on the ordinary stock shall be £4 per cent, per annum, Gas Light and Coke. 46 and the standard price for gas 3s. 3d. per 1,000 cubic feet, and that 14 candles shall be substituted for 16 as the standard illuminating- power. Clause 39 of the scheme for the amalgamation of the company with the London Gas Light Company in 1883 provided that the company should not charge for gas in the districts of the London Gas Light Company south of the Thames a higher price than the price for the time being charged by the South Metropolitan Gas Company for gas of the same illuminating power. The Council petitioned against the Bill with the view of obtaining the insertion of a clause providing that the company shall not charge in their southern district a higher price than that charged by the South Metropolitan Company. The company having agreed to the insertion of such a clause the Council withdrew its opposition to the Bill, which was passed on the 16th August, 1909. 48. This Bill was promoted by riparian owners on the River Wandle with a view to checking the reduction of spring-water by pumping operations by the Croydon Corporation. This Council petitioned in favour of the Bill, and authorized the Medical Officer of Health and Borough Engineer to give evidence in support thereof. The Bill, as passed, provides that the Croydon Corporation shall not sink any well upon, or construct any works for taking or intercepting water from any lands, if such taking or intercepting materially diminishes the flow of water in the Wandle, unless the works and lands upon which the same are to be constructed are specified in an Act or Order confirmed by Parliament; that the Corporation shall not abstract from the Waddon wells more than 50 million gallons of water in every period of 30 days, except so far as they may be hereafter authorized by Parliament, and that they shall keep daily records of the water pumped at Waddon wells. Its object was to make the representation of the people in the House of Commons more nearly proportioned to population by giving to every constituency containing a population of more than 65,000 per member an additional member for every complete 65,000 in excess of the first 65,000, and by enlarging every constituency containing less than 50,000 per member to bring it up over that number, but not over 100,000 per member. This Bill, introduced in 1908, provided that where any Corporation aggregate, or joint stock or other companv, is in occupation of any land or tenement of the yearly value of not less than 10, an officer of such Corporation or Company shall be entitled to be entered in the Local Government Register of Electors and to vote in any election except for a Member of Parliament. This Council approved of the principle of the Bill, but were of opinion that the representation of Companies and Corporations should be in proportion to the rateable value of the premises occupied by them. The Bill passed the House of Lords, and was read a first time in the House of Commons, and then dropped. The Bill has been introduced again this Session, and the Council has petitioned in favour of it. Municipal Franchise (Mercantile Corporations, and Companies). 48 54- This is a Government measure, and proposes to make Part III. of the Housing of the Working Classes Act, 1890, compulsory, deals with the compulsory acquisition of land under Part III. of the Act of 1890, proposes to authorize the Public Works Loan Commissioners to advance loans for the purposes of the Act, to authorize Local Authorities to lay out streets, to authorize the Local Government Board to enforce the execution of the Housing of the Working Classes Acts by Local Authorities, and to abolish the necessity of orders of such Board for the compulsory purchase of land being confirmed by Parliament, to authorize such Board to make inspection and enquiries as to the condition of any area, to amend the procedure for closing and demolition orders, to double the rateable value of premises to which Section 75 of the Act of 1890 applies, and to authorize the Local Government Board to require from Local Authorities reports as to any area and to determine whether the Housing Acts should be put in force in such area. The clauses relating to- town planning provide that Local Authorities may, if authorized by the Local Government Board, prepare schemes with respect to land likely to be used for building purposes, and remove buildings which are not in accordance with the scheme; and that the Local Government Board may order a scheme to be made or carried out in default of the Local Authority. Housing, Town Planning, &c. 55. The Council presented a petition against the Bill, objecting to, among other provisions, those relating to the making of Part III. of the Act of 1890 compulsory, the alteration of the procedure for closing and demolition orders, to the proposed enquiries, the extension of the rateable value for the purpose of Section 75 of the Act of 1890; suggesting that any further legislation dealing with the Housing of the Working Classes Act should be by consolidating and amending the existing law into one Act of Parliament, and stating that whilst in favour of further powers being given to Local Authorities with regard to the width, direction, and levels of streets and other matters in connection with the laying out of land for building purposes, the Council was of opinion that the Town Planning provisions of the Bill would unduly interfere with private rights and would not effect an improvement at all commensurate with the public expenditure which would be involved. 49 56. This Bill proposed to amend the Shop Hours Act, 1904, by making it compulsory on Local Authorities to make closing orders while empowering them to refer to the ratepayers the questions whether any order shall come into operation, and whether any alteration shall be made in the order. This Bill was introduced by the Government, and proposed that rate aid should not be given to nonprovided schools; that the existing law as to Parliamentary grants should be amended; and that trustees of schoolhouses held under charitable trusts might, notwithstanding those trusts, transfer the schoolhouse to the Local Education Authority. The Council presented a petition against the Bill on the following, among other, grounds, viz. : its reactionary character from an educational standpoint, its subversion of trust deeds, and its confiscation of voluntary school buildings. The Bill was read a second time and referred to a Committee of the House of Commons, but was withdrawn before consideration by the Committee. Elementary Education (England and Wales). 59. The Departmental Committee also considered as to making recommendations that Parliament should empower authorities such as the London County Council and this Council to apply to the Privy Council for an Order in Council for the better allotment and administration of coroners' duties, and that the duty now imposed upon inquest juries to view bodies should be abolished. A return, prepared by the London County Council, showing the names of the Managers who, during the year ended 30th June, 1908, had made fewer than three attendances at Meeting's of Managers, and fewer than four visits during school hours to the schools in the group, has been considered by the Council, and the attention of the Council's Managers in question was drawn to the return. The County Council was so informed, and that the Council hoped this might result in better attendances at Managers' Meetings and visits to the schools in future, but felt that until the powers and duties of the Managers were largely increased, and their reasonable requisitions supplied, there would be great difficulty in inducing Managers to take more interest in the work of the schools. Attendances of Managers and Powers and Duties of Managers. 69. The Council decided to support the action of the Bermondsey Borough Council in urging the London County Council to enlarge the powers of School Managers, and appointed delegates to a Conference convened by the Bermondsey Council to consider what further action could be taken in the matter. 25 City and Borough Councils were represented at the Conference, 52 and a resolution was passed to the effect that it was desirable that a closer connection should be established between such Councils and the schools in their respective localities, and urging the London County Council to delegate to the City and Borough Councils greater powers in the management of the schools. The Council wrote to the County Council in support of the resolution, and was informed in reply that it was considered that ample opportunity for Managers to assist the cause of education might be found in the duties assigned to Managers, and that the Committee of the County Council shared the desire to secure the interest of Managers in the schools, but were unable to agree in thinking that the powers and duties already delegated to Managers would fail to secure this end. 70. "Widening Roads across Tooting Common. 85. For the purpose of widening the way across Tooting Common between Church Lane and Rectory Lane, opposite Mantilla Road, two small pieces of the Common were, with the County Council's consent, added to the public way. The Borough Council also proposed that Church Lane should be widened by throwing into the public way two small pieces of Tooting Common at the corners of Mantilla Road. The County Council did not see its way to surrender the piece of the Common at the eastern corner, but arrangements are being made for the piece at the western corner to be added to the public way. 86. With one exception, the whole of the property required for widening Mitcham Road in connection with the construction of electric tramways along that thoroughfare from Tooting Broadway to the County boundary at Tooting Junction railway station, has been acquired, and the land thrown into the public way paved. The piece of forecourt needed to complete the improvement is only a few yards in extent, and, having regard to the high price asked by the owners, the Borough Council concurred in the proposal of the County Council that no further steps should be taken at present for its acquisition. Some of the surplus land purchased in connection with the widening was sold to the London County Council for the purpose of a tramways electricity sub-station, and steps are being taken with the view of the disposal of the remainder. Two-thirds of the cost of the improvement will be borne by the County Council. Miteham Road "Widening. 87. Most of the forecourts required for the widening of York Road, Wandsworth, in connection with the electrification of the tramways there, have been acquired, and the necessary paving works executed. With the view of com- York Boad Widening. 57 pleting the improvement as soon as possible steps are being taken for the compulsory purchase of the outstanding interests in the remaining forecourts. High Street, Wandsworth, and St. Ann's Hill Widening. 88. The London County Council having acquired the site of the old Vicarage in High Street, Wandsworth, for the purpose of erecting a technical institute thereon, the Borough Council offered to transfer its interest in the vacant land and cottages, at the corner of High Street and St. Ann's Hill, to the County Council so as to enlarge the area of land available for the institute, and give it a more important frontage. The offer of the Borough Council was conditional upon the County Council widening to 54 feet the part of High Street upon which the premises abutted, throwing into the public way the site of the bay windows of the cottages in St. Ann's Hill, and contributing two-thirds of the cost of the paving works to be executed in connection with the proposed improvement. The London County Council accepted this offer, an agreement was entered into, and the consents of the Local Government Board and the Board of Education obtained. The necessary steps are being taken with the view of the widening being effected as soon as possible. Footbridge over River Wandle. 89. The new footbridge over the River Wandle, by McMurray's paper mills, Garratt Lane, referred to in last year's report, was constructed at a total cost, including the acquisition of a small piece of land required for the western abutment, of £190 16s. 5d. The estimated cost was £200. The new bridge is in a more convenient position and more commodious than the old one, which has been removed. Putnev Bridge Road Widening go. The Borough Council's applications for contributions towards the cost of widening certain parts of Putney Bridge Road are still awaiting the decision of the London County Council. At the request of the County Council that Council was furnished with a plan showing the widenings which it was suggested should be carried out should a line of tramways be constructed along the road from Putney to Wandsworth, and an estimate of the cost of such widenings is in course of preparation. The County Council promised to consider the Borough Council's applications when this estimate is supplied. 58 9i- The widening of Putney Bridge Road between the London and South-Western Railway bridge and a point near Fawe Park Road was completed at a total cost of £1,847 17s. iid. The estimated cost was £1,700. The County Council has not yet dealt with the Borough Council's application for a contribution towards this improvement. High Street, Putney, Widening. 92. The greater part of the land required for widening High Street, Putney, at Nos. 58 to 68 (even, inclusive) under the agreement entered into with Brandon's Putney Brewery, Limited, in 1903, having been thrown into the public way and paved, the Council came to an arrangement' with the company for the completion of the widening at Nos. 66 and 68 to be postponed for the present, and for the improvement, when executed, to be continued in front of No. 70, High Street, to the corner of Lacy Road. Lower Richmond Road Widening. 93. The completion of this improvement in accordance with the scheme approved by the Council is still in abeyance, difficulties having arisen with regard to certain property required for the widening. The matter is in the hands of the Highways Committee, who will continue to give it their attention. Charlwood Road Widening. 94. The suggested widening of Charlwood Road in connection with the erection of a County Council School in that road at the corner of Hotham Road, referred to in last year's report (paragraphs 129-130), was again the subject of correspondence between the Borough Council and the County Council. The widening of the road to 40 feet having been rendered impossible, except at great cost, by the London County Council erecting the school close to the highway, a proposal was made that sufficient land should be given up to widen the road 20 feet from the centre, the Borough Council executing the necessary paving works. The Borough Council agreed to this modified widening, but the County Council then proposed that the Borough Council should also bear the cost of erecting a new boundary wall to the school. The Borough Council decided to inform the County Council that the question of the erection of the wall was a new point which had not been raised before, and the Borough Council could not entertain the suggestion, and that upon sufficient land being given up to widen the road 20 feet from the centre in front 59 of the school, the Borough Council would execute the necessary paving works free of cost. The matter is now under the consideration of the County Council. West Hill Widening. 95. When the Borough Council decided to widen West Hill, Wandsworth, the estimated cost of the property and paving works, including the cost of widening the road in front of the police station, was £25,000. The London County Council, however, decided that the widening should commence on the western side of the police station, and estimated the cost at £23,800, of which such Council promised to contribute two-thirds, not exceeding £15,866. The total cost of this part of the improvement was £28,457 5s. 3d. The County Council's estimate of the cost was somewhat low, and the excess of the actual over the estimated cost of the improvement was caused chiefly by (a) the large sum awarded by the jury to the sub-lessee and tenant of No. i, West Hill (coffee shop); (6) the cost of acquiring the leasehold interest in Priorsdean House (wheelwright's premises); (c) the amount of the vendor's solicitors' costs and surveyors' fees payable by the Council; and (d) the piece of surplus land between the Public Library and the Convent not yet having been disposed of. This surplus land (part of the sites of Nos. 30 and 32, West Hill) was offered for sale by public auction on two occasions, but was not sold. The approved plan showed a widening at No. 3, West Hill, but, owing to the excessive claims and to the very small strip of property required, the improvement line was re-arranged, additional land being obtained on the opposite side of the road so as to secure the full width of 60 feet without interfering with No. 3. 96. The London County Council was informed of the reasons for the excess of the actual cost over the estimated cost of the improvement, and was asked to increase the amount of its promised contribution. This application is now awaiting the -decision of the County Council. 97. The total cost of widening West Hill at the police station, in accordance with the modified scheme approved by the Council, was 3s. 3d., of which two-thirds (£49 8s. iid.) was contributed by the County Council. The total estimated cost of the improvement was £95. The saving upon the estimate was due to the work of setting back the forecourt fences, etc., costing less than was anticipated. 6o High Street, Clapham, Widening. q8. Terms have now been agreed for the purchase of all the interests proposed to be acquired in the strip of property required for widening High Street, Clapham, and arrangements are being made with the view of the improvement being effected when the leases of the premises expire in 1910. The County Council is contributing one-third of the cost Valley Road Widening. 99. The Council came to an arrangement for the widening to 40 feet of the part of Valley Road, Streatham, between Sunnyhill Road and Wellfield Road. The owner of the property on the eastern side of the road gave up the necessary land and erected a new fence to an approved give-andtake line. The paving works were executed by the Council at its own cost. Tooting Bee Rad and Upper Tooting Rad Widening 100. The total cost of widening Tooting Bec Road and Upper Tooting Road, when the Stapleton House estate was developed for building purposes, was £2,045 4s. 2d. The estimated cost of the improvement was £ 1,900. Unemployment 101. The extension of the sewer in Rectory Lane, and the construction of additional gullies there, formed part of the Rectory Lane scheme, but the Central Body declined to undertake this work, which was executed by the Council at its own expense, the estimated cost being £360. This is not included in the statement above. 104. The Borough Council also submitted to the Central Body a scheme for the excavation of the bed of the Bell Lane Creek, the construction of a concrete embankment wall at the Council's wharf there, and the alteration of the levels of the wharf in connection therewith. The estimated cost of the work was as follows, viz.: unskilled labour, £1,447 i6s. 8d.; skilled labour, £.312 17s. 6d. ; materials, £775 14s.; contingencies, £128 11s. 10d.; total, ,£2,665. The Borough Council offered to provide the necessary materials for the work, and to pay the cost of the skilled labour, but the Local Government Board did not see their way to make a grant to the Central Body to cover the cost of the unskilled labour, and the further consideration of the matter was adjourned. 105. The Borough Council suggested to the London County Council that the work of laying out and embanking the two strips 62 of land between the River Wandle and Garratt Lane, near McMurray's paper mills, and the formation of bowling- greens at Wandsworth Park, Wandsworth Common, and Tooting Common would be suitable work for the unemployed. The County Council concurred in the first-mentioned suggestion, but declined to arrange for the provision of the proposed bowling greens. 106. As in previous years the Council executed, at a cost of about £2,000, a quantity of channelling, kerbing, etc., works, upon which the unemployed were engaged. 107. The Borough Council also lent to the Vacant Land Cultivation Society several small pieces of vacant land in various parts of the Borough for cultivation by the unemployed, and other persons of small means, under the direction of the society. Tooting Bee Boad Widening 108. After repeated applications the London County Council approved the modified proposal of the Borough Council for widening Tooting Bec Road, referred to in last year's report (page 65, paragraph 121), and consented to surrender strips of Tooting Common for this purpose, subject to a post and rail fence being provided on the southern side of the road as well as between the horse ride and the footpath on the northern side, and to the footpath on the Common, south of Tooting Bec Road, being efficiently lighted. These conditions were agreed to by the Borough Council, and, as stated above, the work was carried out in conjunction with the Central (Unemployed) ody. Blackshaw Road Improvement- i09. The widening of Blackshaw Road, Tooting-, between the Lambeth Cemetery and Tooting High Street, has been completed at a total cost of £1,480 6s. id. The estimated cost of this improvement was £1.620. Ravensbury Road and Revelstoke Road. 110. An agreement was entered into with the Wimbledon Corporation as to the maintenance of parts of Merton Road, Ravensbury Road, and Revelstoke Road, Southfield, adjoining the boundary of the Boroughs of Wandsworth and Wimbledon. Coronation Gardens. 111. Applications having been received for permission to play lawn tennis in Coronation Gardens, two courts were provided on the grass plot on the southern side of 63 the gardens. Regulations similar to those in force at Leader's Gardens were made for the use of the courts. Intercepting Traps in House Drains. 112. Towards the end of last year a Departmental Committee was appointed by the President of the Local Government Board to enquire and report with regard to the use of intercepting traps in house drains, and, at the request of the Board, the Council authorized the Borough Engineer and the Medical Officer of Health to give evidence before the committe, if desired House Refuse Removal. 113. In December last the Council again had under consideration the subject of the collection and disposal of house refuse in the Clapham, Streatham, Balham, and Tooting Wards. The work of collection was then carried out by the Council's men and carts and hired horses, the stabling accommodation being provided by the Council. Part of the refuse collected was dealt with at the Council's destructor at Tooting, the remainder being conveyed by rail to shoots in the country. Upon the recommendation of the Highways Committee the Council decided to invite tenders for carrying out the work by contract under the following schedules, viz.:— Schedule No. 1.—Collection and disposal of house refuse from the above-mentioned Wards. Schedule No. 2.—Collection of house refuse from the above-mentioned Wards, and disposal thereof, with the exception of the disposal of about 245 loads per week, to be delivered by the contractor at the dust destructor at Tooting, and to be disposed of by the Council without expense to the contractor. 114. The tenders received having been carefully considered, together with a report by the Borough Engineer as to the cost of the work during the past few years and the estimated cost during the year beginning on the 31st March last, the Committee came to the conclusion that it would be to the advantage of the Council to accept the lowest tenders under Schedule No. 2, the estimated saving being over £1,000 per annum, and the practice of sorting refuse during collection being abolished. The Council concurred in these views, and accepted the following tenders for a period of three years from the 31st March, 1909, viz.:— 64 Schedule No. 2. £ Clapham Wards Mr. J. Guyatt 9,600 Streatham Ward Mr. J. Cronk 7,200 Balham Ward Mr. J. Guyatt 4,500 Tooting Ward Mr. J. Guyatt 3,000 The necessary contracts were entered into, and the work is now being carried out in accordance therewith. 115. The Council's railway wagons, dust vans, etc., which were no longer required, were disposed of advantageously. 117. Having regard to objections which were made to the amount of the Council's charges for permission to advertise on hoardings erected on the public way, the general question of the licensing of these hoardings and the placing of advertisements thereon was reconsidered. After careful enquiry, the Council decided to adhere to the practice of granting licenses for a period of one month, upon payment of a fee of 5s. for each licence; and to reduce the charge in respect of advertisements one-half, i.e., from is. to 6d. per square yard per month in main streets, and from 6d. to 3d. per square yard per month in other streets. The Borough Engineer was authorized to sanction the affixing of advertisements to hoardings, if he sees no objection thereto; and directions were given for a note to be placed at the foot of the licences giving particulars of the Council's charges in the matter. 65 118. Soman Catholic Ground, Wandsworth Cemetery. 121. It having been found that the piece of land at Wandsworth Cemetery set aside for Roman Catholic burials was becoming filled, the Council, with the sanction of the Secretary of State, has allotted a further piece of land for such burials. Randsworth Cemetery. 122. A large shelter has been erected at the entrance to Wandsworth Cemetery, and a new water closet and urinal for men has also been provided. Extension of Cemeteries. 123. The subject of acquiring additional land for burials, to meet future requirements, has been under consideration. Two proposals were before the Council, one for the extension of Streatham Cemetery, and the other for the extension of Putney Vale Cemetery. With regard to the Streatham proposal it was found that only a small area would be available for burials, and the price of the land was considered to be too high. The Council eventually decided to purchase, subject to the approval of the Local Government Board, 15 acres of land (at £400 per acre) adjoining Putney Vale Cemetery, and a provisional agreement for purchase has been entered into. 66 125. Swimming Championship Trophy. 127. The competition for the swimming trophy presented by Sir William Lancaster, J.P., L.C.C., and competed for annually by men resident in the Borough, was held on the 16th September, at the annual entertainment of the Church Institute Swimming Club; entries were received and the trophy was won by Mr. E. F. Ellis. Sir William Lancaster again gave a prize for the winner, as a memento of the occasion, and the Mayor (Alderman Lorden) provided prizes for Mr. Jas. Symons and Mr. A. J. M. Owen, who finished second and third respectively. Women's Medal. 128. The competition for the medal for women residing in the Borough, presented by the late Mr. John Bell, J.P., was held on the 24th September, at the annual 67 entertainment of the ladies' section of the Wandsworth Swimming Club, and was won by Miss N. Treversh. Swimming Competitions for School Children. 129. The Council decided, as an encouragement to children to learn swimming, to arrange competitions and to award a free pass to the second-class bath, available during the following year, to the successful boy or girl from each school attending the baths for instruction in swimming, the passes to be available out of school hours and before seven o'clock in the evening. The competitions were held at the baths on the 23rd October, and were largely attended by children and their parents. Sir William Lancaster, J.P., L.C.C., kindly presided. There are 62 schools in the Borough, 29 departments send pupils to the baths for instruction in swimming, and of these 26 entered for the competitions. The number of children taking part in the competitions was 136—68 boys and 68 girls. Proposed Alterations at the Wandsworth Baths. no. The subject of the use of the first-class swimming bath during the winter season, which, when floored over, has been used as a gymnasium, has been further considered. The building has been let on several occasions during the past winter for a poultry show and whist drives, and for certain purposes appears to supply a want, where the Town Hall would not be available or a less expensive hall is required. Plans and estimates of the cost of the alterations which would be required by the London County Council before a licence would be granted, have been prepared and submitted to theCounty Council for their approval. Proposed Spray Baths at Wandsworth. 131. The subject of the practicability of providing spray baths at the Wandsworth Baths, either by the adaptation of some of the present slipper baths or otherwise, has been further considered, and on the recommendation of the Baths and Washhouses Committee it was decided, in view of the diminution in the number of persons using the slipper baths, not to nrooeed further with the scheme. Lighting at Tooting Baths. 132. A 2,500 candle-power lamp has been provided outside the Tooting Baths in order to improve the lighting there, at a cost of £23 10s. The lights in the men's baths have been re-arranged, and the lighting of the spray chambers improved. 68 APPORTIONMENTS. 133. HENRY GEORGE HILLS, Town Clerk. East Hill, Wandsworth, S.W., August, 1909. 102 Appendix "A." REPORT OF BOROUGH ENGINEER AND SURVEYOR. MILEAGE OF ROADS. The total length of roads repaired by the Council is now 183 miles, 7 furlongs, 143 yards. This does not include 10 miles, 4 furlongs, 153 yards of public ways, which are used as footpaths only. SEWERS. During the past year the following lengths of sewers, &c., have been constructed in the Borough:— Totals. Lineal feet of new sewers 6,122 Manholes 24 Gullies 187 The defective 12-inch pipe sewer between Danmere Street and the Embankment has been taken up and relaid. The work was carried out under contract by Mr. J. E. Etheridge at a cost of £138 4s. Ashlone Road. The ditch at the rear of No. 39 has been filled in and piped with 12-inch pipes at a cost of £12 7s. 7d. Tooting High Street. The dead end of the 9-inch pipe sewer opposite No. 204 has been connected to the manhole opposite Ravenna Road at a cost of £19 12s. 4a. Upper Bichmond Road. SEWER VENTILATION. Sewer ventilating shafts have been fixed against sides of houses and columns erected during the year, in lieu of surface ventilators in the roads which in all cases have been hermetically sealed. 103 The total number of ventilating shafts and columns are as follows, viz.:— 397 6-inch by 4-inch ventilating shafts. 1 4-inch by 4-inch do. 2 4-inch by 3 inch do. 78 6-inch circular do 40 5-inch do. do. 61 4 inch do. do. 3 3-inch do. do. 116 6-inch ventilating columns 698 PARTICULARS OF NEW SEWERS. New treads have been fixed on the steps at the underground convenience. High Street, Putney, by the Safety Tread Syndicate Limited, at a cost of £15 13s. 11d. A new underground convenience for men has been constructed in Christchurch Road at the junction with Brixton Hill. The accommodation provided is two W.C.s, eight urinal stalls, lavatory compartment and attendant's room. The work was carried out under contract by Mr. A. A. Sedcole, the total cost, including the diversion of 18-inch water main being £1,193 8s. 6d. PRIVATE DRAINS. Tree planting 81 19 1 193 18 2 275 17 3 724 9 6 148 16 2 1,626 10 11 Garratt Park culvert 617 4 3 767 0 0 1,384 4 3 753 5 3 Rectory Lane— Alterations to gradients 1,121 10 11 285 2 0 1,406 12 11 1,096 6 7 339 17 0 1,436 3 7 £ 1,820 14 3 1,246 0 2 3,066 14 5 1,820 16 1 1,241 18 5 3,062 14 6 The following resolution was adopted by the Council with reference to the value of the work — "We have considered the letter, dated 24th June, from the Clerk, Central (Unemployed) Body for London, relative to the works of altering gradients in Rectory Lane, Streatham and Tooting, and culverting ditch at Garratt Park, Springfield, recently executed with unemployed labour, asking for the opinion of the Council upon the quality of the work, the conduct of the men generally, and as to the value of the labour furnished by the Central Body compared with ordinary labour, and report of the Borough Engineer thereon; and recommend that the Central (Unemployed) Body be informed (1) that the quality of the work, all of which was set out and superintended by the Council's Engineer, was fairly good ; (2) that the conduct of the men was satisfactory; and (3) that the value of the labour furnished depended upon the class of work required of the men, and was approximately as follows, viz.:—alteration of gradients, Rectory Lane, cost 30 per cent. more than ordinary labour ; construction of culvert, Garratt Park, cos-t 50 per cent. more than ordinary labour, and that it was found necessary to have the works closely supervised, and this was done by men in the employ of the Council." 110 NEW STREETS. General Report on Testing of Gas supplied (I) by the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company; (2) by the Mitcham and Wimbledon Gas Company, during the year ended March 31st, 1909. Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company. During the whole of this year, ended March 31st, 1909, in accordance with instructions which I received from the Council, and which came into force on July 1st, 1907, I have tested the gas supplied by this Company on two days weekly at irregular intervals, and have occasionally made extra tests, instead of making daily tests as I had previously done from October, 1903, to June, 1907. The Tables appended, showing averages of illuminating power sulphur and pressure, and the curves (in Table III.), indicating the fluctuations of the first two, are therefore based on these less frequent testings. The times of testing, however, are still those laid down by the somewhat antiquated Gas Works Clauses Act, 1871 (with an extension of one hour in advance of those times by special arrangement with the Company in 1906), viz., from April to September inclusive, between 8.0 and 11.0 p.m., and from October to March inclusive, between 5.0 and 10.0 p.m. I mention this point as I understand that some members of the Council are of opinion that the gas, like other Metropolitan gas, should be tested at all reasonable times; an opinion which I have frequently urged in the past, with only slight success so far. Another reason for reviving this contention is the possibility that at some future date the Council might desire to make tests of the calorific power, and it is generally felt that, as regards these, no limit as to time of testing would be reasonable; since gas ntay be used for heating and other purposes at any time of the day or night. I will refer to this point later in connection with recent legislation. Wandsworth Borough Council. Table III, showing Weekly Averages of Illuminating Power and Sulphur of Gas supplied by the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company from bi-weekly testings at Disraeli Road, Putney from April l?t 1908. to March 1909. 137 Illuminating Power. The illuminating power has varied much as usual between 14.5 and 15.5 candles, seldom being lower than I4.5 and occasionally only somewhat higher than 15.5 candles, with a general average of 14.9 candles, for the year ended March 31st, 1909. The statutory limit is 14.0 candles. Table I. shows the monthly averages, and in Table III. a curve is given showing the weekly fluctuations in the illuminating power. Tests with flat-flame burners have not been made, and it may be remarked that the use of this form of burner is becoming rapidly less as time goes on. Sulphur. The average amount of sulphur (other than sulphuretted hydrogen) in the gas has considerably increased during the year ended March 31st, 1909, being 29.5 grains in 100 cubic feet of gas, as compared with an average of 25.6 grains for the previous year. Table I. shows the monthly averages of this constituent of the gas, and indicates a variation between 22 8 grains (March, 1909), and 39.7 grains (July, 1908). In Table III. a curve is drawn which indicates the fluctuations of sulphur from week to week. From this Table it will be seen that the highest amounts occurred between July and October, 1908 (the average for these four months being 35 grains) the maximum point (43.9 grains) being reached during the week ending July 25th, 1908. During the last five months of the year ended 31st March, 1909, however, it decreased, the average from November, 1908, to March, 1909, being only 25.4 grains. Sulphuretted Hydrogen. There has been no sulphuretted hydrogeu found in the gas at any testing, during the year ended March 31st, 1909. Pressure. From Table I., which shows the monthly averages of pressure based on bi-weekly observations, it will be seen that these averages have varied between 2.4 inches (December, 1908) and 3.2 inches (July, 1908), the general average for the whole year ended March 31st, 1909, being 2.8 inches. I made a special Report to the Council on the subject of pressure, in December, 1908. 138 Calorific Power and recent Legislation. Tests of the calorific power of the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company's gas have not hitherto been made, as it was felt by the Council that they would prefer to await the results of tests made by the London County Council which were commenced in January, 1906. Since that date, daily tests have been made of the calorific power of the gas supplied by the Metropolitan Gas Companies, and it is considered that the time has now arrived when a standard calorific power can safely be fixed. The increasing use of gas for heating and cooking, for small fuel purposes in certain manufactories, for motor power, and especially also for illuminating purposes in incandescent burners, coupled with the steadily decreasing use of flat-flame burners, all tend to emphasise the importance of testing the calorific power of gas. Although from experiments made, there seems to be, so far, no very clearly defined relation between calorific power and illuminating power, it would appear that, ceteris paribus, a gas of high calorific power will give a greater illumination than one of lower calorific power. As a practical outcome of long continued experiments, a clause has been inserted by agreement, after conference between the Gas Light and Coke Company and the London County Council (in a Bill which has recently passed the Committee stage of the House of Commons, authorising the acquisition of the undertaking of the West Ham Gas Company by the Gas Light and Coke Company), fixing the standard of calorific power at 125 calories net (see Miuutes of Proceedings, L.C.C., March 23rd, 1909, p. 672). It is also generally agreed that the calorific power, if tested at all, should be tested at all reasonable times, since the gas may be used for heating and other purposes both by day and night. Mitch am and Wimbledon Gas Company. As pointed out in my last Annual Report on Gas Testings made during the year ended March 31st, 1908, the testings of the gas supplied by this Company at the new testing place in Haydon's Road, South Wimbledon, instead of at the Works of the Company as heretofore, commenced in January, 1908, in accordance with the Mitcham 139 and Wimbledon Gas Act, 1907, and have since been there continued during the whole of the year ended March 31st, 1909. Illuminating Power. The standard illuminating power is 14.0 caudles, but the testings have indicated, on the whole, a much higher figure. Thus Table II., which gives the results of all fortnightly testings made, shows the yearly average to be 16.0 candles, while the lowest result indicated is 14.9 candles. The pressure has varied between 2.6 and 4.2 inches, with a Pressure. general average of 3.3 inches. Sulphuretted Hydrogen. There has been no sulphuretted hydrogen found in the gas at any testing during the year ended March 31st, 1909. H. Wilson Hake, Ph.D., Gas Examiner. 140 TABLE I. Clerk. 30th june, 1909. 182 Appendix "F." REPORT OF THE WANDSWORTH DISTRESS COMMITTEE. The Distress Committee was appointed by the Borough Council nn the 11th Ontober. 1905. in accordance Appointment- with the Unemployed Workmen Act (1905), and constituted as follows :— Members of the Borough Council 12 Members of the Board of Guardians8 Persons experienced in the relief of distress5 Members of Committee- Members of the Council:—Aldermen Anderson, Hewett, Lorden, Penfold, and Robinson ; Councillors Cresswell, Couzens, Danielli, Eastwood, Fletcher, Jackson, and Taylor. Members of the Board of Guardians :—Mr. C. Brodie, Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Councillor W. P. Mellhuish, Mr. P. Messent, Mr. Percival Rees (Vice-Chairman), Lieut. E. A. Sanders, R.N., and Mr. A. Sullivan. Members experienced in the relief of distress, appointed for one year :—Mr. C. Colman, Rev. D. Tudor Craig, Mr. A. Glegg, J.P. (Chairman), Mr. T. Jones, and Miss M. H. Pollock. Sub-Cornmittee and Reference. A Sub-Committee of twelve members was formed, constituted as follows :—Mr. Percival Rees (Chairman); Councillors Cresswell, Danielli, Fletcher, and Jackson, Lieut. Sanders, R.N., Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. C. Brodie, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Mr. T. Jones, and the Chairman and Members of the Central Body, ex-officio; the duties being to enquire and report 183 as to the conditions of labour, to consider and classify the Record Papers when completed. Reception at Office. Applications from unemployed persons were received at the office of the Distress Committee, 3, Church Row, The Plain, Wandsworth, during- the winter months, from Men on Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday, and from Women on Wednesday, between the hours of 9 a.m. and 12 o'clock noon. Investigation. The particulars entered on the Record Papers were investigated and verified by personal visits to the homes of the applicants by the investigators, and references as to character were obtained from previous employers. No personal investigations were made outside the Borough. Classification. The Sub-Committee considered the completed Record Papers and classified the applications into four divisions :— Preference, Eligible, Ineligible, and Disqualified. In recommending applicants to the Central Body as suitable for employment, migration, or emigration, the Sub-Committee gave preference to men of good character, and distinguished as far as possible, between the habitual "out of work," and the applicant who was unemployed through trade depression, or kindred causes. Payment of Wages. The wages of the men from this Borough employed on the Non-Colony Works were paid on Saturday morning at the Office of the Committee; the week's work being from Monday morning to Friday night. The rate of wages was 6d. per hour. Family Allowance- The men sent to the Working Colonies receive 6d. per week, in addition to their board and lodging, a weekly allowance being made to the family on the following scale :—10s. to the wife, 2s. for the first child under 14, is. 6d. for the second child under 14, and is. for each other child under 14 years; but in no case was 17s. 6d. to be exceeded. The allowances are paid at the homes of the men on Wednesdays. The men are allowed a furlough at the end of each month, their fares being paid for them. M 184 Representatives of Wandsworth on the Central (Unemployed) Body for London. Rev. J. H. Anderson, M.A., Chairman of Works Committee. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Works Committee, 77.7 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of the Finance Committee, 28.5 per cent. Of the work-people applying in 1908-9 :— 52 applied in 1905-6 only 10 given work. 53 ,, 1906-7 17 „ 261 ,, 1907-8 89 „ 37 „ 1905-6 and 1906-7 14 „ 25 „ 1905-6 and 1907-8 8 „ 35 „ 1906-7 and 1907-8 13 „ 41 „ 1905-6, 1906-7 and 1907-8 22 „ Number of applicants whose cases were rendered eligible by Local Government Board Order, dated 17th November, 1908, rescinding disqualifications as to Poor Law Relief and work in two preceding years—20. Number of such applicants submitted and approved and given work—7. 192 Effect of the Provision of Work. The effect produced upon those who obtained work, through the medium of the Distress Committee, varied according to the character of the applicant. In the case of those anxious to work and keep their homes together it was noticeable that after a week's wages, when nourishing food had been obtained, they gradually improved in efficiency. Advantages of Colony Work. Colony work has the advantage of fresh air and healthy surroundings, and of removing men from many local temptations. For various reasons, a number of applicants have declined to leave their homes for any period, preferring to wait for local employment. Experience in Administering the Act. In administering the Act the Committee found reason to believe that a false impression was created amongst the unemployed, who, after having had the enquiry forms filled up and having received visits from the Investigators as to the correctness of the statements, felt that work was certain. As only 425 out of 1,756 applicants obtained 9 weeks' work, the disappointed balance lost confidence in the usefulness of the Act, and to some extent also in those administering it. The impression that work was coming also slackened their efforts to obtain employment elsewhere. Volunteers. The Committee has not availed itself of the services of additonal voluntary workers. Preliminary Investigation. The Committee had referred to them before investigation all cases where there appeared to be a technical disqualification, and if the applicant did not comply with the regulations issued by the Local Government Board no further action was taken. Applications from single men and married men without families were not investigated, unless the application was for Emigration. 193 The foregoing remarks are the same in substance as those made last year. An additional year's experience confirms the opinions of the Committee then expressed. ALEX. GLEGG, Chairman. PERCIVAL REES, Vice-Chairman. TWENTY-SECOND ANNUAL REPORT: 1st April, 1908, to 31st March, 1909. SUB-COMMITTEE, 1909. Alderman H. BULCRAIG, J.P. (Chairnuui). Councillor A. D. DAWNAY, J.P. (Mayor). Councillor J. W. CUNDALL. REED WELCH. 198 ANNUAL REPORT OF THE SUB-COMMITTEE OF CLAPHAM PUBLIC LIBRARY, For the Year ended 31st March, 1909. The Sub-Committee have pleasure in presenting the TwentySecond Annual Report on the work of the Clapham Library. The number of books issued during the year was 125,278 in the Lending Library and 6,198 in the Reference Library (exclusive of books in open cases), being a total issue of 131,476 volumes, and a daily average issue of 539 volumes. These figures are much higher than those for any year since the library was opened, and show an increase of issues of 17,631 volumes over the previous year, and a daily average increase of 78 volumes issued. The number of books now in stock is 18,198, of which 14,820 are in the Lending Library and 3,378 in the Reference Library. Advantage has been taken of the preparation of a new catalogue of works of fiction and juvenile literature (to be published in the forthcoming summer) to weed out a number of obsolete and worn-out books. 3,973 readers' ordinary tickets (including renewals) and 947 students' tickets were issued during the year. The issue of students' tickets has been very successful, and, no doubt, accounts to some extent for the large increase in the number of books taken out. The Sub-Committee desire to express their cordial thanks to the various donors of books, periodicals, pictures, etc., during the past year. The Sub-Committee regret that, owing to the theft of several books from the open cases in the Reference Library, they have been reluctantly compelled to discontinue placing books on shelves accessible to the public. 199 The Borough Council in November, 1908, appointed the Mayor (Councillor Dawnay), Alderman Bulcraig, and Councillors Cundall, Downer, Law, Monday, and Richardson, as the Sub-Committee for the Clapham Library for 1909. Alderman Bulcraig was elected chairman, and a vote of thanks was passed to Councillor Downer for his services as chairman during the previous year. Councillor W. E. Law, a member of the Sub-Committee, died on :8th March, and the Committee passed a sincere vote of condolence with the family. The only change in the staff was the appointment of H. Hetherington as a junior assistant in February. The Sub-Committee desire to express their entire satisfaction with the excellent manner in which the Librarian and his Staff have performed their duties, and especially with the services of the assistants during the absence, through illness, of Mr. Welch, in November and December last. On behalf of the Sub-Committee, HENRY BULCRAIG, Chairman. 3rd May, 1909.
